        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the current research project, we have prepd. a novel Sb@C nanosphere anode with biomimetic yolk-shell structure for Li/Na-ion batteries via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement route.  The yolk-shell microstructure consists of Sb hollow yolk completely protected by a well-conductive carbon thin shell.  The substantial void space in the these hollow Sb@C yolk-shell particles allows for the full vol. expansion of inner Sb while maintaining the framework of the Sb@C anode and developing a stable SEI film on the outside carbon shell.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb@C coaxial nanotubes as a superior long-life and high-rate anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhiming; Yu, Xin-Yao; Lou, Xiong Wen; Paik, Ungyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.  With different annealing time, the hollow space and the amt. of Sb inside the tube can be easily tuned by the partial evapn. of Sb.  The as-obtained Sb@C nanotubes exhibit excellent sodium storage properties.  The remarkable electrochem. performance results from the unique coaxial nanoarchitecture.  Specifically, it delivers a high specific capacity of 407 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 240 cycles.  Furthermore, a stable capacity of 240 mAh g-1 can be retained at 1.0 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles.  Most importantly, high capacities of 350 mAh g-1 and 310 mAh g-1 can be achieved at large current densities of 10 and 20 A g-1, resp., which represents the best rate performance among the reported Sb-based anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmon6HTiU9LrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhF7oaBshahzw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a top alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of Na-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the development of anode materials for SIBs to date was mainly limited to carbonaceous materials with minimal research devoted to high capacity alloy-based materials.  An Sb/C electrode with ∼30 nm Sb nanoparticles (NPs) uniformly encapsulated in interconnecting 1-dimensional (1D) 400 nm C fibers (denoted as SbNP@C) was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.  This binder-free, current collector-free SbNP@C electrode demonstrated high capacity and stable long-term cycling performance at various current densities.  The SbNP@C electrode showed an initial total capacity of 422 mA-h/gelectrode and retained 350 mA-h/gelectrode after 300 deep charge-discharge cycles under 100 mA/gSb.  Also, because of the efficient 1-dimensional Na-ion transport pathway and the highly conductive network of SbNP@C, the electrode preserved high overall capacities even when cycled at high currents, extending its usability to high power applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCf3y1wC4rXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhF7oaBshahzw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWht7nJ&amp;md5=382586ead9328ea5a3721bf05276e705</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/batt.201800014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Navarro-Suárez, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Soln.-processable two-dimensional (2D) materials offer the possibility of manufg. heterostructures with various properties, creating a way to tune materials towards a specific application.  Two different 2D materials, titanium carbide MXene (Ti3C2Tx) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO), have shown promising results for supercapacitor applications due to their flake-like morphol., high cond.; and ability to intercalate mols. or ions for charge storage.  Here, we demonstrate the self-assembly of a heterostructure between neg. charged Ti3C2Tx and pos. charged modified rGO after shear mixing.  Changes in zeta (ζ) potential, X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns; and Raman spectra confirm the assembly of this heterostructure.  The produced rGO : Ti3C2Tx heterostructures were used as electrodes for supercapacitors.  The addn. of rGO to Ti3C2Tx allowed some widening of the voltage window.  Moreover, due to the synergistic effect of these materials, an increase of the capacitance value was obsd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We present a general and rational approach to fabricate highly accessible and affordable sodium-ion battery anodes by engineering three-dimensional hydrogenated Na2Ti3O7 nanoarrays supported on flexible Ti substrates.  The hydrogenated Na2Ti3O7 nanoarrays exhibit desirable properties for sodium storage, such as high surface area, high elec. cond., and Na+ diffusivity.  The as-obtained nanoarrays demonstrate remarkably stable and robust Na-storage performance when tested as binder-free anodes for sodium-ion battery. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2259</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2265</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201504412</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D2259-2265%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DJ.%2BNi%26author%3DS.%2BFu%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DJ.%2BMaier%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26title%3DSelf-Supported%2BNanotube%2BArrays%2Bof%2BSulfur-Doped%2BTiO2%2BEnabling%2BUltrastable%2Band%2BRobust%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201504412&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.0c04366&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201504412&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Supported Nanotube Arrays of Sulfur-Doped TiO2 Enabling Ultrastable and Robust Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Fu, Shidong; Wu, Chao; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2259-2265</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We, for the 1st time, combine the unique nanotubular architecture with high cond. by engineering self-supported nanotube arrays of S-doped TiO2 (S-TiO2).  Such doping by isovalent substitution can be helpful owing to either elastic effect or, at high enough concn., to variation of materials const. (e.g., bandgap).  S-doped TiO2 materials have been reported and characterized, yet never used as electrodes for Na-based battery behaviors.  The increase of electronic cond. could be predominately ascribed to structure affects rather than proper doping, as shown by the strong effect on the band gap.  An addnl. possibility is the introduction of an anionic deficiency (anion vacancies compensated by electron due to prepn.).  Note the deoxygenation effect of S treatment, an aliovalent effect as, e.g., achieved by donor doping TiO2, may be excluded here.  The S-TiO2 nanotube array features intrinsic merits for Na storage.  First, the self-supported nanotube array can be directly adapted for electrode without using binder and C additive.  Second, the ordered nanotube architecture exhibits large interface and channels for transfer of Na ion during cycling.  Third, the S doping drastically boosts the electron movement within the nanotubes.  Consequently, the S-TiO2 nanotubes enable superior Na storage in terms of high capacity (320 mAh/g), ultrastable cycling (91% retention over 4400 cycles), and robust rate capability (167 mAh/g at 3.35 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrObwc1x3fRibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg3Cv9jMxUl0w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1ektbc%253D&amp;md5=cf8583f1f9e0593bbc7f6af9a5227e30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201910043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dual-Doped Hematite Nanorod Arrays on Carbon Cloth as a Robust and Flexible Sodium Anode</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dual-Doped Hematite Nanorod Arrays on Carbon Cloth as a Robust and Flexible Sodium Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Menglei; Wang, Zhenzhu; Ni, Jiangfeng; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1910043</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries with flexibility can find tremendous applications in wearable and bendable electronics.  One central mission for the advancement of such high-performance batteries is the exploration of flexible anodes with electrochem. and mech. robustness.  Herein reported is a robust and flexible sodium-ion anode based on self-supported hematite nanoarray grown on carbon cloth.  The ammonia treatment that results in dual doping of both nitrogen and low-valent iron renders surface reactivity and elec. cond. to the material.  The dual-doped hematite arrays afford a robust activity for sodium storage, exhibiting reversible capacities of 895 and 382 mAh g-1 at current rates of 0.1 and 5 A g-1, resp., or 615 and 356 mAh g-1 by removing the contribution of the substrate.  They also sustain 85% of the initial capacity upon 200 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  To demonstrate the flexibility, full cells composed of a hematite array anode and Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode are assembled.  The cell is capable of affording an energy d. of 201 Wh kg-1 and sustaining repeated bending without performance decay, demonstrating a significant potential in practical application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6gV3UBkCpnLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg3Cv9jMxUl0w"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rooting binder-free tin nanoarrays into copper substrate via tin-copper alloying for robust energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Zhu, Xiaocui; Yuan, Yifei; Wang, Zhenzhu; Li, Yingbo; Ma, Lu; Dai, Alvin; Li, Matthew; Wu, Tianpin; Shahbazian-Yassar, Reza; Lu, Jun; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The need for high-energy batteries has driven the development of binder-free electrode architectures.  However, the weak bonding between the electrode particles and the current collector cannot withstand the severe vol. change of active materials upon battery cycling, which largely limit the large-scale application of such electrodes.  Using tin nanoarrays electrochem. deposited on copper substrate as an example, here we demonstrate a strategy of strengthening the connection between electrode and current collector by thermally alloying tin and copper at their interface.  The locally formed tin-copper alloys are electron-conductive and meanwhile electrochem. inactive, working as an ideal "glue" robustly bridging tin and copper to survive harsh cycling conditions in sodium ion batteries.  The working mechanism of the alloy "glue" is further characterized through a combination of electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, at. structural anal. and in situ X-ray diffraction, presenting itself as a promising strategy for engineering binder-free electrode with endurable performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWEPmwP-Db8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg3Cv9jMxUl0w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXlt1Sgsb4%253D&amp;md5=62308ee499fbe492b1ed0ba633ca3852</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201901096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Template-Free Construction of Self-Supported Sb Prisms with Stable Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Monodisperse Antimony Nanocrystals for High-Rate Li-ion and Na-ion Battery Anodes: Nano versus Bulk</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Meng; Kravchyk, Kostiantyn; Walter, Marc; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report colloidal synthesis of Sb nanocrystals with mean size tunable in the 10-20 nm range and with narrow size distributions of 7-11%.  In comparison to microcryst. Sb, 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals exhibit enhanced rate capability and higher cycling stability as anode materials in rechargeable Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  All three particle sizes of Sb have high and similar Li-ion and Na-ion charge storage capacities of 580-640 mA-h/g at moderate charging/discharging current densities of 0.5-1C (1C rate is 660 mA/g).  At all C-rates (0.5-20C, e.g. current densities of 0.33-13.2 A/g), capacities of 20 nm Sb particles are systematically better than for both 10 nm and bulk Sb.  At 20C rate, retention of charge storage capacities by 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals can reach 78-85% of the low-rate value, indicating that rate capability of Sb nanostructures can be comparable to the best Li-ion intercalation anodes and is so far unprecedented for Na-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5xNSHYkxGf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhABHwt8X9Dsw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs1Wmsbw%253D&amp;md5=6c9a0c090f52077a9b8eda7847cbfe2f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.01.033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bio-Inspired Engineering of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>-PPy Yolk-Shell Composite for Highly Durable Lithium and Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>33</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">213</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">220</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bio-inspired engineering of Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite for highly durable lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Haichen; Ni, Jiangfeng; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">213-220</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth based compds. are uniquely interesting as anode materials in energy storage devices such as rechargeable batteries, owing to their large volumetric capacity and suitable operating potential higher than graphite.  How to achieve the high capacity durably and robustly remains an open challenge.  To address this issue, here we propose a bio-inspired material engineering of yolk-shell composite that consists of bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) nanowire assembly intimately encapsulated in polypyrrole (PPy) shell.  The Bi2S3 yolk features a large void space and a short diffusion distance, while the PPy shell is highly conductive, flexible and resilient, allowing for the free vol. variation upon ion uptake and release.  When used as anode, the Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite exhibits a superior Li storage cyclability (99% for 500 cycles) and a high rate capability (337 mAh g-1 at 10 C), outstripping any previous bismuth based materials.  This composite also affords a high reversible capacity of 591 mAh g-1 and a favorable durability for Na storage.  The discrepancy between Li and Na storage may correlate to the larger vol. change of Bi alloying with Na (∼250%) against with Li (∼110%).  This work offers a potential creative approach to engineering efficient electrodes for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGovto5xM8CXa7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhABHwt8X9Dsw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXit1Squ7Y%253D&amp;md5=949f4f32dff24a1486a9f12104b2d489</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.02.041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bismuth Chalcogenide Compounds Bi<sub>2</sub>X<sub>3</sub> (X = O, S, Se): Applications in Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">356</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">366</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bismuth chalcogenide compounds Bi2×3 (X=O, S, Se): Applications in electrochemical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Bi, Xuanxuan; Jiang, Yu; Li, Liang; Lu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth chalcogenides Bi2×3 (X=O, S, Se) represent a unique type of materials in diverse polymorphs and configurations.  Multiple intrinsic features of Bi2×3 such as narrow bandgap, ion cond., and environmental friendliness, have render them attractive materials for a wide array of energy applications.  In particular, their rich structural voids and the alloying capability of Bi enable the chalcogenides to be alternative electrodes for energy storage such as hydrogen (H), lithium (Li), sodium (Na) storage and supercapacitors.  However, the low cond. and poor electrochem. cycling are two key challenges for the practical utilization of Bi2×3 electrodes.  Great efforts have been devoted to mitigate these challenges and remarkable progresses have been achieved, mainly taking profit of nanotechnol. and material compositing engineering.  In this short review, we summarize state-of-the-art research advances in the rational design of diverse Bi2×3 electrodes and their electrochem. energy storage performance for H, Li, and Na and supercapacitors.  We also highlight the key tech. issues at present and provide insights for the future development of bismuth based materials in electrochem. energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvPe7r_HhOybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhABHwt8X9Dsw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktVCht70%253D&amp;md5=3a06450975bea75cb931620e2fc5de15</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b00616"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Capacity, High-Rate Bi–Sb Alloy Anodes for Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-based anodes have recently aroused much attention in sodium ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their high theor. capacities and low sodiation potentials.  However, their progresses are prevented by the inferior cycling performance caused by severe volumetric change and pulverization during the (de)sodiation process.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Natural structural materials are built at ambient temp. from a fairly limited selection of components.  They usually comprise hard and soft phases arranged in complex hierarchical architectures, with characteristic dimensions spanning from the nanoscale to the macroscale.  The resulting materials are lightwt. and often display unique combinations of strength and toughness, but have proven difficult to mimic synthetically.  Here, we review the common design motifs of a range of natural structural materials, and discuss the difficulties assocd. with the design and fabrication of synthetic structures that mimic the structural and mech. characteristics of their natural counterparts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7crvDsCD9B7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifRoGTrjgaIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSqtr%252FK&amp;md5=c685610f7a7a726a4c7c07c8f269bfa0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1038/nature19060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luna, P.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced electrocatalytic CO2 reduction via field-induced reagent concentration</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Min; Pang, Yuanjie; Zhang, Bo; De Luna, Phil; Voznyy, Oleksandr; Xu, Jixian; Zheng, Xueli; Dinh, Cao Thang; Fan, Fengjia; Cao, Changhong; Garcia de Arquer, F. Pelayo; Safaei, Tina Saberi; Mepham, Adam; Klinkova, Anna; Kumacheva, Eugenia; Filleter, Tobin; Sinton, David; Kelley, Shana O.; Sargent, Edward H.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">537</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7620</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">382-386</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NATUAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0028-0836</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. redn. of CO2 (CO2) to CO (CO) is the 1st step in the synthesis of more complex C-based fuels and feedstocks using renewable electricity.  Unfortunately, the reaction suffers from slow kinetics owing to the low local concn. of CO2 surrounding typical CO2 redn. reaction catalysts.  Alkali metal cations are known to overcome this limitation through noncovalent interactions with adsorbed reagent species, but the effect is restricted by the soly. of relevant salts.  Large applied electrode potentials can also enhance CO2 adsorption, but this comes at the cost of increased H (H2) evolution.  Here we report that nanostructured electrodes produce, at low applied overpotentials, local high elec. fields that conc. electrolyte cations, which in turn leads to a high local concn. of CO2 close to the active CO2 redn. reaction surface.  Simulations reveal 10-fold higher elec. fields assocd. with metallic nm-sized tips compared to quasi-planar electrode regions, and measurements using Au nanoneedles confirm a field-induced reagent concn. that enables the CO2 redn. reaction to proceed with a geometric c.d. for CO of 22 mA per square centimeter at -0.35 V (overpotential of 0.24 V).  This performance surpasses by an order of magnitude the performance of the best Au nanorods, nanoparticles and oxide-derived noble metal catalysts.  Similarly designed Pd nanoneedle electrocatalysts produce formate with a faradaic efficiency of &gt;90 per cent and an unprecedented geometric c.d. for formate of 10 mA per square centimeter at -0.2 V, demonstrating the wider applicability of the field-induced reagent concn. concept.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQayNCUPlg37Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifRoGTrjgaIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1yqsbzO&amp;md5=11d8dcf8010b105587ba93d7035bc657</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1038/s41560-019-0402-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Haleem, Y.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomically dispersed platinum supported on curved carbon supports for efficient electrocatalytic hydrogen evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Daobin; Li, Xiyu; Chen, Shuangming; Yan, Huan; Wang, Changda; Wu, Chuanqiang; Haleem, Yasir A.; Duan, Sai; Lu, Junling; Ge, Binghui; Ajayan, Pulickel M.; Luo, Yi; Jiang, Jun; Song, Li</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Dispersing catalytically active metals as single atoms on supports represents the ultimate in metal utilization efficiency and is increasingly being used as a strategy to design hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) electrocatalysts.  Although platinum (Pt) is highly active for HER, given its high cost it is desirable to find ways to improve performance further while minimizing the Pt loading.  Here, we use onion-like nanospheres of carbon (OLC) to anchor stable atomically dispersed Pt to act as a catalyst (Pt1/OLC) for the HER.  In acidic media, the performance of the Pt1/OLC catalyst (0.27 wt% Pt) in terms of a low overpotential (38 mV at 10 mA cm-2) and high turnover frequencies (40.78 H2 s-1 at 100 mV) is better than that of a graphene-supported single-atom catalyst with a similar Pt loading, and comparable to a com. Pt/C catalyst with 20 wt% Pt.  First-principle calcns. suggest that a tip-enhanced local elec. field at the Pt site on the curved support promotes the reaction kinetics for hydrogen evolution.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJrrQmHUiMvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifRoGTrjgaIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtVyqt7fL&amp;md5=2c299fa0dfff9e24b843813fdd48b7e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1039/b922875f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structural Control of a Cobalt Nanocone Array Grown by Directional Electrodeposition</span>. <i>CrystEngComm</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2799</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2802</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile Synthesis of Hierarchical Iron Phosphide/Biomass Carbon Composites for Binder-Free Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Hui; Li, Xueying; Chen, Lizhuang; Dan, Yuanyuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Batteries &amp; Supercaps</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Seeking a simple direct construction strategy for transition-metal-phosphide-based composites as anodes for sodium-ion batteries is attracting great attention for the development of high-performance sodium-ion batteries.  In this work, we design iron phosphide nanosheets grown on a biomass carbon membrane by a facile electrodeposition method, followed by an annealing process.  The biomass carbon membranes as three dimensional frameworks, possessing initial biol. structures from Magnolia leaves, do not only improve the cond. of the electrodes but also relieve iron phosphide aggregation during the charging-discharging processes.  The iron phosphide nanosheets could increase the accessible surface area for electrochem. reactions, further promoting the storage of sodium ions.  Due to the unique structure of the iron phosphide nanosheets/biomass carbon membrane, the electrodes exhibit 500.9 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 500 mA g-1, the electrodes still retain 197 mAh g-1 after a long-time test (500 cycles).                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Anode Performance of in Situ Formed Cu2Sb Nanoparticles Integrated on Cu Foil via Replacement Reaction for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Liubin; Wang, Chenchen; Zhang, Ning; Li, Fujun; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">256-262</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A scalable and binder-free Cu2Sb/Cu electrode has been synthesized via replacement reaction as an anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The thickness of Cu2Sb formed on Cu foil can be facilely tuned by adjusting the concn. of Sb3+ and reaction time.  A high capacity of 318.4 mAh g-1 is obtained at 0.08 A g-1, and a capacity retention of 98.5% is also maintained after 200 cycles at 0.8 A g-1.  The reaction mechanism of the as-synthesized Cu2Sb/Cu is investigated by using ex situ X-ray diffraction and transmission electron microscopy.  The porous Cu2Sb nanoparticle film and its intrinsic contact with the Cu foil result in the good electrochem. performance.  This facile synthetic route for the integrity of Cu2Sb nanoparticles and Cu foil allow for simplifying the prepn. processes of SIBs in large-scale applications and is applicable for advanced material design and synthesis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq3laGJFKcxcbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbAudm5Tevdg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGgtbvL&amp;md5=2ca013127d177ab487715ca2336804f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/batt.201900082"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Battery-Type Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Batteries &amp; Supercaps</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">899</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">917</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Battery-Type Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Xiaoyu; Zhang, Yingbing; Wang, Yanfei; Wei, Huige</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Batteries &amp; Supercaps</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion capacitors (NICs), as a new type of hybrid energy storage devices, couples a high capacity bulk intercalation based battery-style neg. (or pos.) electrode and a high rate surface adsorption based capacitor-style pos. (or neg.) electrode, delivering high energy d., high power d., and long lifespan.  Since the first NICs have been proposed in year 2012, numerous efforts have been put into searching for appropriate electrode materials to compose NICs devices with improved performance.  Esp., battery-type electrode materials carry greater responsibility on performance improvement of NICs.  This review provides an overview of electrode materials for NICs according to energy storage mechanisms with an emphasis on battery-type electrode materials design and improved NICs performance.  Further, future challenges and perspectives of NICs are also discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGraZlPYyBP5QLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbAudm5Tevdg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFemsr3I&amp;md5=34ce1e939aee2583b70064c9cf5021d6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bard, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A math. model describing ionic transport in a 3D-microbattery (3D-MB) electrolyte is developed here using finite element methodol.  The model is then exploited to study a 3D-MB based on an interdigitated plate ("trench") architecture for a 10 μm-thick electrolyte layer sepg. 10 μm-thick graphite anode and LiCoO2 cathode plates.                 10.1007/s12274-017-1536-0</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D3189-3201%26journal%3DNano%2BRes.%26author%3DL.%2BLiang%26author%3DY.%2BXu%26author%3DL.%2BWen%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BZhou%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BZhao%26author%3DU.%2BKaiser%26author%3DY.%2BLei%26title%3DHierarchical%2BSb-Ni%2BNanoarrays%2Bas%2BRobust%2BBinder-Free%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-Ion%2BHalf%2Band%2BFull%2BCells%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs12274-017-1536-0&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.0c04366&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs12274-017-1536-0&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Sb-Ni nanoarrays as robust binder-free anodes for high-performance sodium-ion half and full cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Liying; Xu, Yang; Wen, Liaoyong; Li, Yueliang; Zhou, Min; Wang, Chengliang; Zhao, Huaping; Kaiser, Ute; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3189-3201</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel hierarchical electrode material for Na-ion batteries composed of Sb nanoplates on Ni nanorod arrays is developed to tackle the issues of the rapid capacity fading and poor rate capability of Sb-based materials.  The three-dimensional (3D) Sb-Ni nanoarrays as anodes exhibit the synergistic effects of the two-dimensional nanoplates and the open and conductive array structure as well as strong structural integrity.  Further, their capacitive behavior is confirmed through a kinetics anal., which shows that their excellent Na-storage performance is attributable to their unique nanostructure.  When used as binder-free sodium-ion battery (SIB) anodes, the nanoarrays exhibit a high capacity retention rate (more than 80% over 200 cycles) at a c.d. of 0.5 A·g-1 and excellent rate capacity (up to 20 A·g-1), with their capacity being 580 mAh·g-1.  Moreover, a P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2//3D Sb-Ni nanoarrays full cell delivers a highly reversible capacity of 579.8 mAh·g-1 over 200 cycles and an energy d. as high as 100 Wh·kg-1.  This design strategy for ensuring fast and stable Na storage may work with other electrode materials as well.[Figure not available: see fulltext.].</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVvOsDNAjidrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbAudm5Tevdg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXos1aku7s%253D&amp;md5=727a2351515bb6b07ad1485f102a9228</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1002/cey2.12"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Demanding Energy from Carbon</span>. <i>Carbon Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">8</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">12</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/cey2.12</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D1%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D8-12%26journal%3DCarbon%2BEnergy%26author%3DY.%2BYuan%26author%3DJ.%2BLu%26title%3DDemanding%2BEnergy%2Bfrom%2BCarbon%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fcey2.12&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.0c04366&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fcey2.12&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.  Although existing energy storage is dominated by pumped hydroelec., there is the recognition that battery systems can offer a no. of high-value opportunities, provided that lower costs can be obtained.  The battery systems reviewed here include sodium-sulfur batteries that are com. available for grid applications, redox-flow batteries that offer low cost, and lithium-ion batteries whose development for com. electronics and elec. vehicles is being applied to grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZwDymuubZm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lian4lVkM7kAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsVGktL%252FJ&amp;md5=5035bfda7631ad9d075e8836e61146ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703137"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Delmas, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium and Sodium-Ion Batteries: 50 Years of Research</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Portable electronic devices (PEDs) are promising information-exchange platforms for real-time responses.  Their performance is becoming more and more sensitive to energy consumption.  Rechargeable batteries are the primary energy source of PEDs and hold the key to guarantee their desired performance stability.  With the remarkable progress in battery technologies, multifunctional PEDs have constantly been emerging to meet the requests of our daily life conveniently.  The ongoing surge in demand for high-performance PEDs inspires the relentless pursuit of even more powerful rechargeable battery systems in turn.  In this review, we present how battery technologies contribute to the fast rise of PEDs in the last decades.  First, a comprehensive overview of historical advances in PEDs is outlined.  Next, four types of representative rechargeable batteries and their impacts on the practical development of PEDs are described comprehensively.  The development trends toward a new generation of batteries and the future research focuses are also presented.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqgtoghhfCp0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglRqd8kjiqxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVKnsbnM&amp;md5=87afe7c5c7ecd491e83e778be8936d3f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/batt.201800057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Werner, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Apaydin, D. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Portenkirchner, E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Anthraquinone/Carbon Fiber Composite as Cathode Material for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Batteries &amp; Supercaps</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">160</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">168</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/batt.201800057</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Anthraquinone/Carbon Fiber Composite as Cathode Material for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Werner, Daniel; Apaydin, Dogukan H.; Portenkirchner, Engelbert</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Batteries &amp; Supercaps</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">160-168</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">BSAUBU</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The transition from rare to natural abundant materials in rechargeable batteries is becoming a grand challenge in developing a resource sustainable power supply.  Since decades, scientists attempt to circumvent the lithium's resource problem by innovating alternative active metal ions.  A cost-effective alternative to lithium is to use sodium (Na) as the carrier ion in rechargeable batteries.  We present an electrode composite material comprising anthraquinone (AQ) and nanostructured carbon fibers, as a cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  These electrodes are characterized by a large surface area, ordered porous network, large pore vol. and good elec. cond.  The material is further compared to the water sol., mono-substituted anthraquinone deriv., sulfonated 9,10-anthraquinone (SAQ).  While the SAQ/carbon fiber composite demonstrates a moderate initial discharge capacity of ∼95 mAh g-1 accompanied by substantial, initial capacity fading, the AQ/carbon fiber composite shows a remarkably high discharge capacity of ∼307 mAh g-1 and exhibit reasonable cycling stability over 115 charge/discharge cycles in a Na contg. electrolyte.  This may be best explained by the well-structured intermol. π-π stacking of the thermally evapd. AQ layers and with the subjacent carbon fibers.  Since AQ and SAQ are widely-used industrial pigments, they may offer a cost-effective, abundant and environmentally benign cathode material for secondary Na-ion and Na-flow batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpUqUL4GUokCLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglRqd8kjiqxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjsV2rur0%253D&amp;md5=6f21fbf14ddb44ba5aa42c954468d12a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/cey2.32"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rhee, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J. H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Black Tio<sub>2</sub>: What Are Exact Functions of Disorder Layer</span>. <i>Carbon Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">44</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">53</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/cey2.32</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Black TiO2: What are exact functions of disorder layer</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sungsoon; Cho, Yoonjun; Rhee, Ryan; Park, Jong Hyeok</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">44-53</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEANFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2637-9368</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Australia, Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Among the substantial amt. of photocatalyst materials, TiO2 has been enthusiastically studied for a few decades due to its outstanding photocatalytic activity and stability.  Recently, black TiO2 consisting of approx. 2 nm of thin disorder layer around the surface showed surprisingly high solar hydrogen generation ability.  The disorder layer of TiO2 can enhance its light absorption, charge sepn., and surface reaction abilities, however exact fundamentals of photocatalytic water-splitting pathways are still ambiguous.  Herein, recent progress and investigations on exact functions of disorder layer and its application in photocatalytic CO2 redn. will be discussed.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) that efficiently store electricity into chem. energy have been extensively pursued because of their great potential for low-cost and large-scale stationary application such as smart grid and renewable energy.  Successful deployment of SIBs requires efficient anode materials that could store Na+ ions via a reversible way at reasonable rates.  Materials based on antimony and bismuth are capable of storing a high-concn. of Na+ ions via a reversible alloying reaction at suitable redox potentials, and thus have drawn substantial attention.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa). Consequently, as a sodium-ion battery anode, the SbNPs@3D-C delivers a high reversible capacity (456 mAh/g at 100 mA/g), stable cycling performance (94.3% capacity retention after 500 cycles at 100 mA/g) as well as superior rate capability (270 mAh/g at 2000 mA/g). Free from expensive template sources and complex manipulation, this work might shed some light on the synthesis of low-cost and high-performance materials for the next "beyond lithium" battery generation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpYqJH9BlxHCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguDon5LIS8nQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFWktLzO&amp;md5=3fc4643288a77027dd91444fa9926cb6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201501313"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb Nanoparticles Encapsulated in a Reticular Amorphous Carbon Network for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5381</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5387</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb@3D RCN (Reticular Carbon Network) films were prepd. through electrostatic spray deposition.  The encapsulating nanosized Sb in reticular porous carbon network enables excellent storage properties with respect to Na.  More specifically, at 0.2 C the Sb@3D RCN film electrode delivers a reversible capacity of 630 mA h g-1, approaching 96% of its theor. capacity.  Cycle stability tests conducted at a rate of 3 C exhibit a reversible capacity of 224 mA h g-1 after 900 cycles.  This performance is attributed to the unique Sb@3D RCN: (i) the carbon matrix prevents Sb nanoparticles agglomeration upon prolonged cycling; (ii) the large void space within 3D RCN may buffer the vol. expansion, leading to the high cycling stability of the electrode material; and (iii) the reticular structure ensures fast transport of the electrolyte within the electrode. Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a top alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of Na-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the development of anode materials for SIBs to date was mainly limited to carbonaceous materials with minimal research devoted to high capacity alloy-based materials.  An Sb/C electrode with ∼30 nm Sb nanoparticles (NPs) uniformly encapsulated in interconnecting 1-dimensional (1D) 400 nm C fibers (denoted as SbNP@C) was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Soln.-processable two-dimensional (2D) materials offer the possibility of manufg. heterostructures with various properties, creating a way to tune materials towards a specific application.  Two different 2D materials, titanium carbide MXene (Ti3C2Tx) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO), have shown promising results for supercapacitor applications due to their flake-like morphol., high cond.; and ability to intercalate mols. or ions for charge storage.  Here, we demonstrate the self-assembly of a heterostructure between neg. charged Ti3C2Tx and pos. charged modified rGO after shear mixing.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We, for the 1st time, combine the unique nanotubular architecture with high cond. by engineering self-supported nanotube arrays of S-doped TiO2 (S-TiO2).  Such doping by isovalent substitution can be helpful owing to either elastic effect or, at high enough concn., to variation of materials const. (e.g., bandgap).  S-doped TiO2 materials have been reported and characterized, yet never used as electrodes for Na-based battery behaviors.  The increase of electronic cond. could be predominately ascribed to structure affects rather than proper doping, as shown by the strong effect on the band gap.  An addnl. possibility is the introduction of an anionic deficiency (anion vacancies compensated by electron due to prepn.).  Note the deoxygenation effect of S treatment, an aliovalent effect as, e.g., achieved by donor doping TiO2, may be excluded here.  The S-TiO2 nanotube array features intrinsic merits for Na storage.  First, the self-supported nanotube array can be directly adapted for electrode without using binder and C additive.  Second, the ordered nanotube architecture exhibits large interface and channels for transfer of Na ion during cycling.  Third, the S doping drastically boosts the electron movement within the nanotubes.  Consequently, the S-TiO2 nanotubes enable superior Na storage in terms of high capacity (320 mAh/g), ultrastable cycling (91% retention over 4400 cycles), and robust rate capability (167 mAh/g at 3.35 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrObwc1x3fRibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgscsdq-nUICw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1ektbc%253D&amp;md5=cf8583f1f9e0593bbc7f6af9a5227e30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201910043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dual-Doped Hematite Nanorod Arrays on Carbon Cloth as a Robust and Flexible Sodium Anode</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries with flexibility can find tremendous applications in wearable and bendable electronics.  One central mission for the advancement of such high-performance batteries is the exploration of flexible anodes with electrochem. and mech. robustness.  Herein reported is a robust and flexible sodium-ion anode based on self-supported hematite nanoarray grown on carbon cloth.  The ammonia treatment that results in dual doping of both nitrogen and low-valent iron renders surface reactivity and elec. cond. to the material.  The dual-doped hematite arrays afford a robust activity for sodium storage, exhibiting reversible capacities of 895 and 382 mAh g-1 at current rates of 0.1 and 5 A g-1, resp., or 615 and 356 mAh g-1 by removing the contribution of the substrate.  They also sustain 85% of the initial capacity upon 200 cycles at 0.2 A g-1.  To demonstrate the flexibility, full cells composed of a hematite array anode and Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode are assembled.  The cell is capable of affording an energy d. of 201 Wh kg-1 and sustaining repeated bending without performance decay, demonstrating a significant potential in practical application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6gV3UBkCpnLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgscsdq-nUICw"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rooting binder-free tin nanoarrays into copper substrate via tin-copper alloying for robust energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Zhu, Xiaocui; Yuan, Yifei; Wang, Zhenzhu; Li, Yingbo; Ma, Lu; Dai, Alvin; Li, Matthew; Wu, Tianpin; Shahbazian-Yassar, Reza; Lu, Jun; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The need for high-energy batteries has driven the development of binder-free electrode architectures.  However, the weak bonding between the electrode particles and the current collector cannot withstand the severe vol. change of active materials upon battery cycling, which largely limit the large-scale application of such electrodes.  Using tin nanoarrays electrochem. deposited on copper substrate as an example, here we demonstrate a strategy of strengthening the connection between electrode and current collector by thermally alloying tin and copper at their interface.  The locally formed tin-copper alloys are electron-conductive and meanwhile electrochem. inactive, working as an ideal "glue" robustly bridging tin and copper to survive harsh cycling conditions in sodium ion batteries.  The working mechanism of the alloy "glue" is further characterized through a combination of electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, at. structural anal. and in situ X-ray diffraction, presenting itself as a promising strategy for engineering binder-free electrode with endurable performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWEPmwP-Db8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lirkavOEy7YIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXlt1Sgsb4%253D&amp;md5=62308ee499fbe492b1ed0ba633ca3852</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201901096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Template-Free Construction of Self-Supported Sb Prisms with Stable Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report colloidal synthesis of Sb nanocrystals with mean size tunable in the 10-20 nm range and with narrow size distributions of 7-11%.                         rightTab-cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bio-inspired engineering of Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite for highly durable lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Haichen; Ni, Jiangfeng; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth based compds. are uniquely interesting as anode materials in energy storage devices such as rechargeable batteries, owing to their large volumetric capacity and suitable operating potential higher than graphite.  How to achieve the high capacity durably and robustly remains an open challenge.  To address this issue, here we propose a bio-inspired material engineering of yolk-shell composite that consists of bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) nanowire assembly intimately encapsulated in polypyrrole (PPy) shell.  The Bi2S3 yolk features a large void space and a short diffusion distance, while the PPy shell is highly conductive, flexible and resilient, allowing for the free vol. variation upon ion uptake and release.  When used as anode, the Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite exhibits a superior Li storage cyclability (99% for 500 cycles) and a high rate capability (337 mAh g-1 at 10 C), outstripping any previous bismuth based materials.  This composite also affords a high reversible capacity of 591 mAh g-1 and a favorable durability for Na storage.  The discrepancy between Li and Na storage may correlate to the larger vol. change of Bi alloying with Na (∼250%) against with Li (∼110%).  This work offers a potential creative approach to engineering efficient electrodes for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGovto5xM8CXa7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lirkavOEy7YIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXit1Squ7Y%253D&amp;md5=949f4f32dff24a1486a9f12104b2d489</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.02.041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bismuth Chalcogenide Compounds Bi<sub>2</sub>X<sub>3</sub> (X = O, S, Se): Applications in Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">356</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">366</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth chalcogenides Bi2×3 (X=O, S, Se) represent a unique type of materials in diverse polymorphs and configurations.  Multiple intrinsic features of Bi2×3 such as narrow bandgap, ion cond., and environmental friendliness, have render them attractive materials for a wide array of energy applications.  In particular, their rich structural voids and the alloying capability of Bi enable the chalcogenides to be alternative electrodes for energy storage such as hydrogen (H), lithium (Li), sodium (Na) storage and supercapacitors.  However, the low cond. and poor electrochem. cycling are two key challenges for the practical utilization of Bi2×3 electrodes.  Great efforts have been devoted to mitigate these challenges and remarkable progresses have been achieved, mainly taking profit of nanotechnol. and material compositing engineering.  In this short review, we summarize state-of-the-art research advances in the rational design of diverse Bi2×3 electrodes and their electrochem. energy storage performance for H, Li, and Na and supercapacitors.  We also highlight the key tech. issues at present and provide insights for the future development of bismuth based materials in electrochem. energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvPe7r_HhOybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lirkavOEy7YIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktVCht70%253D&amp;md5=3a06450975bea75cb931620e2fc5de15</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b00616"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Capacity, High-Rate Bi–Sb Alloy Anodes for Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. redn. of CO2 (CO2) to CO (CO) is the 1st step in the synthesis of more complex C-based fuels and feedstocks using renewable electricity.  Unfortunately, the reaction suffers from slow kinetics owing to the low local concn. of CO2 surrounding typical CO2 redn. reaction catalysts.  Alkali metal cations are known to overcome this limitation through noncovalent interactions with adsorbed reagent species, but the effect is restricted by the soly. of relevant salts.  Large applied electrode potentials can also enhance CO2 adsorption, but this comes at the cost of increased H (H2) evolution.  Here we report that nanostructured electrodes produce, at low applied overpotentials, local high elec. fields that conc. electrolyte cations, which in turn leads to a high local concn. of CO2 close to the active CO2 redn. reaction surface.  Simulations reveal 10-fold higher elec. fields assocd. with metallic nm-sized tips compared to quasi-planar electrode regions, and measurements using Au nanoneedles confirm a field-induced reagent concn. that enables the CO2 redn. reaction to proceed with a geometric c.d. for CO of 22 mA per square centimeter at -0.35 V (overpotential of 0.24 V).  This performance surpasses by an order of magnitude the performance of the best Au nanorods, nanoparticles and oxide-derived noble metal catalysts.  Similarly designed Pd nanoneedle electrocatalysts produce formate with a faradaic efficiency of &gt;90 per cent and an unprecedented geometric c.d. for formate of 10 mA per square centimeter at -0.2 V, demonstrating the wider applicability of the field-induced reagent concn. concept.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQayNCUPlg37Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liBq_uOKXUAMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1yqsbzO&amp;md5=11d8dcf8010b105587ba93d7035bc657</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1038/s41560-019-0402-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Haleem, Y.
